Witnesses Required for Nafaqah of Found Animal
Explains necessity of witnesses for nafaqah of found animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the requirement of witnesses for the finder to give nafaqah by judge's order, and explain the rational basis for this requirement.

Core Idea
Without witnesses, a finder's possession of a lost animal is presumed ghasp, not amanah.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies a critical condition for the finder of a lost animal who wishes to give nafaqah (expenditure) by order of the judge and later seek reimbursement from the owner. The key is establishing that the finder took the animal with the intention of returning it (amanah) rather than keeping it (ghasp). The judge requires witnesses to confirm this intention. Let us explore the ruling and its rational proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is the finder (multaqit) giving nafaqah (food, shelter) to a found animal by order of the judge. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) for the finder to do so once the judge orders it, but only if the finder first establishes witnesses to prove the animal was taken as an amanah.
Without the judge's order, the finder may still feed the animal voluntarily but cannot claim reimbursement.
2
Locate the Condition
The condition for the finder to give nafaqah by judge's order is that witnesses are established to confirm the finder's intention of returning the animal. This condition comes from Imam Muhammad's Mabsut, a foundational text of the Hanafi school.
The condition is specific to seeking reimbursement; general ta'rif (announcement) is for returning the animal to the owner.
3
Analyze the Rational Proof (Dalil Aqli)
The proof is rational: if the finder takes the animal without witnesses, his possession is indistinguishable from ghasp (usurpation). The default presumption in Islamic law is that possession of another's property without proof of trust is unlawful. Therefore, witnesses are necessary to rebut this presumption.
This is a form of istihsan (juristic preference) based on preventing harm and ensuring justice.
4
Distinguish Ta'rif from Formal Witness
Ta'rif (announcing the find) is sufficient to make the public witnesses when returning the animal to its owner. However, for the judge to order nafaqah, formal witnesses are needed because the finder is claiming a right to reimbursement. Ta'rif alone does not prove the finder's intention at the moment of taking.
The passage emphasizes that if the finder took the animal without ta'rif, his action is haram and equivalent to ghasp.
5
Determine the Judge's Procedure
The judge will say to the finder: 'If you are truthful (i.e., you took it as an amanah), then give nafaqah to the animal; otherwise you are a usurper.' The judge's order is contingent on the finder's ability to bring witnesses. If the finder cannot, the judge will not order nafaqah, and the finder must bear the expense voluntarily if he fed the animal.
This procedure protects the owner's rights and prevents fraudulent claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب اللقطة

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هفتم الا اصل امام محمد کی مبسوط) کی شرط کی رو سے نقطہ کو نفقہ دینے کے حوالے سے قاضی کے حکم کیلئے ملفظ پر گواہ قائم کرنا مشروط ہوگا۔ تا کہ لقطہ جانور کی امانت کا تحقق ہو سکے۔ چنانچہ اگر ملتقط نے گواہ قائم کر دیئے تو بحکم قاضی وہ (ملتقط ) لقطہ جانور کو فقہ دے گا اور مالک سے خرچہ واپس لے گا۔

۴۔ احتمال غصب کی بحث اگر ملتقط ( لقطہ پانے والا ) نے گواہ قائم نہ کئے تو اس میں غصب کا احتمال پایا جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ جب کوئی لفظ حاصل ہوتا ہے تو نہ صرف اس کی تعریف و تشہیر کی جاتی ہے بلکہ لوگوں کو مخاطب کر کے یہ اعلان بھی کیا جاتا ہے کہ جس کا یہ لقطہ ہو وہ مجھ سے لے جائے۔ چنانچہ مالک کو لقطہ واپس کرنے پر لوگوں کو گواہ کرنے کیلئے صرف تعریف و تشہیر کا عمل کافی ہے۔ اگر ملقط نے اپنی ذات کے لئے لقطہ اخذ کیا اور تعریف و تشہیر کا اہتمام نہیں کیا تو اس کا یہ عمل نہ صرف حرام ہے بلکہ لقطہ غصب کرنے کے مترادف ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ لفظہ کو امانت ثابت کرنے اور احتمال غصب کو دور کرنے کے لئے گواہ ضروری ہیں۔ اگر ملتقط نے گواہ پیش نہیں کئے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا سر کسل[؟] (ملتقط ) نے لقہ کو اپنی ذات کے لئے اٹھایا تھا جو کہ تحقیق غصب کو تق (ثابت) کرتا ہے۔ چنانچہ کشف حال کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ لفقط کو امانت ثابت کیا جائے تا کہ قاضی صحیح صورت حال سامنے آنے پر درست فیصلہ کر سکے۔ اس لئے قاضی ملتقط کو یہ کہے گا کہ اگر تو (ملقط ) اپنے قول میں سچا ہے تو ( لقطہ جانور ) کو نفقہ دے ورنہ وہ (ملتقط ) غاصب متصور ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ ملتقط گواہ پیش کرنے سے قاصر ہو۔
The chapter of Luqata. According to the condition from Imam Muhammad's Mabsut, for the finder to give nafaqah by the judge's order, establishing witnesses is conditional, so that the trustworthiness of the found animal can be confirmed. So if the finder establishes witnesses, then by the judge's order he will give nafaqah to the found animal and take back the expense from the owner.

4. Discussion of the possibility of ghasp: If the finder does not establish witnesses, then there is a possibility of ghasp in this. Because when a found object is obtained, not only is it to be defined and announced, but people are addressed with the announcement that whoever this found object belongs to should take it from me. So for returning the found object to the owner, making people witnesses is sufficient through the action of definition and announcement. If the finder took the found object for his own self and did not arrange definition and announcement, then this action of his is not only haram but is equivalent to usurping the found object. This is why witnesses are necessary to establish trustworthiness and remove the possibility of ghasp. If the finder does not bring witnesses, then it means that the person (finder) took the found object for his own self, which confirms ghasp. So for uncovering the situation, it is necessary that the found object be established as a trust so that the judge can make a correct decision upon seeing the true situation. Therefore, the judge will say to the finder: If you are truthful in your statement, then give nafaqah to the found animal, otherwise you will be considered a usurper, provided that the finder is unable to bring witnesses.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the conditions under which a finder of a lost animal can give nafaqah (expenditure) by order of the judge. The key point is that to avoid being considered a usurper (ghasp), the finder must establish witnesses to prove that he took the animal with the intention of returning it to its owner (amanah). The judge's order to give nafaqah is contingent upon this proof. The passage also clarifies that merely announcing the find (ta'rif and tasheer) is sufficient for making people witnesses when returning the animal, but if the finder takes the animal without announcing, his action is haram and equivalent to ghasp. The reasoning is rational: without witnesses, the finder's possession is presumed to be for himself, thus usurpation.

Key Terms
ملتقط (multaqit): The person who finds and picks up a lost item (luqata).
نفقہ (nafaqah): Expenditure for maintaining a found animal, such as feeding and shelter.
غصب (ghasp): Unlawfully taking possession of someone else's property without right.
تعریف و تشہیر (ta'rif wa tasheer): Announcing and making known the found object to the public.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a finder of a lost animal does not establish witnesses, what is the legal status of his possession?
A) Amanah
B) Ghasp
C) Mubah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
A finder of a lost animal must establish witnesses to prove amanah before a judge can order nafaqah; without witnesses, the possession is deemed ghasp.

The Ruling on Nafaqah for Found Property: Distinguishing Sahih and Asahh in Hanafi Fiqh
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nafaqah for found property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sahih and asahh narrations in Hanafi fiqh and explain the ruling that a judge must explicitly make nafaqah a debt for the finder to reclaim it.

Core Idea
The asahh (more authentic) opinion is that the judge must declare nafaqah a debt; otherwise the finder cannot reclaim expenses.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, the author clarifies a key textual reference in Hidayah where the word 'kitab' points to Quduri's Mukhtasar. The central issue is whether the judge's order for nafaqah on a found animal must explicitly designate it as a debt (dayn) for the finder to recover his expenses. This dispute is resolved by distinguishing between two levels of authority: sahih (authentic) from Imam Muhammad's Mabsut and asahh (more authentic) from Quduri. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for applying the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? The judge ordering nafaqah for found property. The ruling is that the finder can reclaim nafaqah if the judge makes it a debt.
The act is a judicial order, not a private transaction.
2
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Two positions: sahih from Imam Muhammad (emphasizing witnesses) and asahh from Quduri (emphasizing debt declaration).
Both are Hanafi; the dispute is within the school.
3
Examine the dalil for each position
The passage cites Quduri's statement 'wa ja'ala al-nafaqata daynan 'ala sahibiha' for the asahh. The sahih is from Imam Muhammad's Mabsut focusing on witnesses.
Quduri's text is the matn; Imam Muhammad's is the original source.
4
Apply the Hanafi tarjih mechanism
The asahh is more emphatic than sahih, so it is mufta bihi (operative ruling).
Tarjih is based on the principle that asahh outweighs sahih.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If judge merely orders nafaqah without debt declaration, the finder cannot reclaim the cost.
This affects the finder's financial risk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۵ عبارت قدوری کی بحث مذکورہ زیر بحث صورت کے حوالے سے ہدایہ کے متن میں لفظ ”کتاب“ سے ایک عبارت کا تذکرہ ہے جس پر احتمال کا تحقق ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ "کتاب" سے مراد قدوری ہے اور اس میں احتمالی عبارت یہ ہے۔ قَولُهُ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَ جَعَلَ النَّفَقَةَ دَيْنًا عَلَى صَاحِبِهَا ( کتاب میں جو یہ فرمایا کہ قاضی یہ نفقہ اس کے مالک پر قرض قرار دے ) اس قول میں یہ اشارہ ہے کہ جب ملتقط حاضر ہو۔ لفظ کا جانور فروخت نہ کیا گیا ہو اور قاضی نے نفقہ کا حکم دے دیا تو متفقطع ( لفظ پانے والا ) جانور کے مالک سے اپنا خرچ واپس لینے کا مجاز ہے۔ بشرطیکہ قاضی نے بطور قرضہ مالک سے رجوع کو مشروط کیا ہو۔ یعنی قاضی نے صرف نفقہ دینے کا حکم دیا اور اسے قرض قرار نہیں دیا تو ملقط نفقہ کا خرچ واپس لینے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ اگر قاضی نے لقطہ جانور کے لئے ملتقط کو نفقہ کا حکم دیتے وقت اسے (نفقہ کو ) قرض قرار دیا تو وہ (ملتقط ) مالک سے واپس لینے کا استحقاق رکھتا ہے اور یہی قول اصح ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہدایہ کے مصنف نے قولہ فی الکتاب سے اصح قول نقل کیا ہے۔ - صحیح واصح کی بحث مذکورہ زیر بحث صورت پر بنی ہدایہ کے متن میں مذکور عبارت کے اندر امام محمد کی مبسوط (الاصل) کے حوالے سے صحیح قول ( برائے مسئلہ قیام شہادت) پیش کیا ہے۔ اور اسی ( زیر بحث ) صورت کے آخر میں قولہ فی الکتاب (قدوری ) کے حوالے سے اصح قول ( در مسئلہ نفقہ برائے قرض ) ذکر کیا ہے۔ (جن کی تفصیلی بحث پہلے گزر چکی ہے چنانچہ صحیح قول سے بہ یفتی ، الفتوی علیہ سے زیادہ مؤکد قول مراد ہے۔ یا کسی قول کا صحیح ہونا اغلب واکثر کے اعتبار سے ہے چنانچہ امام محمد نے الاصل ( مبسوط ) میں قیام شہادت کے قول کو صحیح قرار دے کر زیادہ غالب واکثر رائے کی طرف متوجہ کیا ہے۔ اور قدوری میں نفقہ کو مالک پر قرض قرار دینے کے قول کو صح " کہا گیا ہے جو صحیح کے مقابلے میں زیادہ مؤکد متصور ہوتا ہے۔

خلاصہ کلام یہ کہ یہ یفتی ، الفتویٰ علیہ سے زیادہ موزوں ھوا صیح پر مبنی قول ہوتا ہے اور صحیح کے مد مقابل ” اصح پر مبنی تول زیادہ وزن رکھتا ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
5. Discussion of Quduri's text: Regarding the mentioned scenario, the text of Hidayah mentions a phrase from the word 'kitab', with which possibility is realized. So 'kitab' refers to Quduri, and the possible phrase is: 'His statement in the book: and he made the nafaqah a debt upon its owner.' In this statement is the indication that when the finder is present, the found animal has not been sold, and the judge has ordered nafaqah, then the finder is allowed to take back his expense from the owner, provided the judge made the return conditional as a debt. That is, if the judge only ordered nafaqah and did not declare it a debt, then the finder is not permitted to take back the expense. If the judge, when ordering nafaqah for the found animal, made it a debt, then he (the finder) has the right to take back from the owner, and this is the asahh saying. From this it is known that the author of Hidayah transmitted the asahh saying from 'qawluhu fi al-kitab'.

Discussion of sahih and asahh: In the mentioned scenario from the text of Hidayah, the sahih saying (regarding the issue of establishing witnesses) is presented from Imam Muhammad's Mabsut (al-Asl). And at the end of this scenario, the asahh saying (regarding the issue of nafaqah as a debt) is mentioned from Quduri. (Their detailed discussion has already passed. So from 'sahih' is meant a saying that is more emphatic than 'fatwa' and 'al-fatwa 'alayhi'. Or the correctness of a saying is in terms of predominant. So Imam Muhammad in al-Asl (Mabsut) declared the saying of establishing witnesses as sahih, thereby turning to the more predominant and majority opinion. And in Quduri, the saying of making nafaqah a debt on the owner is called 'sah' [asahh], which is considered more emphatic compared to sahih.

Summary: The saying based on 'sahih' is more suitable than 'fatwa' and 'al-fatwa 'alayhi', and the saying based on 'asahh' carries more weight than 'sahih'. And Allah knows best the correctness.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains a textual reference in Hidayah where the word 'kitab' refers to Quduri's text. It discusses the ruling that when the judge orders nafaqah for a found animal, he must explicitly make it a debt (dayn) upon the owner for the finder to have the right to reclaim it. The passage contrasts two opinions: the 'sahih' (authentic) from Imam Muhammad's Mabsut concerning the requirement of witnesses, and the 'asahh' (more authentic) from Quduri's text concerning making nafaqah a debt. The commentary clarifies that 'asahh' is more emphatic than 'sahih'. The conclusion is that the fatwa is based on the opinion that is more emphatic (asahh).

Key Terms
کتاب (kitab): Here, 'kitab' refers to the text of Quduri (Mukhtasar al-Quduri).
صحیح (sahih): Authentic saying; here from Imam Muhammad's Mabsut.
اصح (asahh): More authentic saying; here from Quduri's text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the judge explicitly making nafaqah a debt?
A) It is not required.
B) It is the asahh position and thus mufta bihi.
C) It is only recommended.
D) It is not from Quduri.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, asahh narrations override sahih when both exist; for nafaqah on found property, the judge must explicitly declare it a debt for the finder to reclaim.

Finder's Right to Detain Found Animal for Nafaqah
Ruling with proof via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the finder's right to detain a found animal until nafaqah is paid and explain the qiyas to the return of a runaway slave.

Core Idea
The finder may detain the found animal until reimbursed for expenses, akin to the case of a runaway slave.

When a person finds a lost animal and incurs expenses to care for it, the owner's appearance raises the question of reimbursement. This lesson examines the ruling from Al-Hidayah: the finder may detain the animal until the owner pays the nafaqah. The reasoning draws an analogy to the finder of a runaway slave, who also may detain the slave until compensated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the hukm: when the owner appears, the finder has the right (ja'iz) to detain the animal until the owner pays the nafaqah.
This right is established even without a prior court order.
2
Understand the reasoning (ishbah bil-bay')
The text says the finder 'gave life' to the animal through his expenses, making it as if the finder acquired ownership from the owner. This resembles a sale where the expense is the price.
This is a legal fiction (taqdir) to justify detention.
3
Analyze the qiyas to radd al-abiq
The finder of a runaway slave may also detain the slave until paid. The 'illa (effective cause) is the expenditure for preservation of property. Apply this 'illa to the found animal case.
Both cases involve voluntary preservation of someone else's property.
4
Distinguish the effect of detention on extinguishment of debt
If the animal perishes before detention, the debt remains. If it perishes after valid detention, the debt extinguishes because the animal becomes like a rahn (pawn).
Detention transforms the finder's possession from a trust (amanah) to a possessory security.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِذَا حَضَرَ يَعْنِى الْمَالِكُ فَلِلْمُلْتَقِطِ أَنْ يَسْتَعَهَا مِنْهُ حَتَّى يَحْضُرَ النَّفَقَةَ لِأَنَّهُ يُحْيِي بِنَفَقَتِهِ فَصَارَ كَأَنَّهُ اسْتَفَادَ الْمِلْكَ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ فَاشْهَ الْمَيْعَ وَأَقْرَبُ مِنْ ذَالِكَ رَادَ الا بِقِ فَإِنَّ لَهُ الْحَيْسُ لا سُتِفَاءِ الْجُعِلِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا ثُمَّ لا يَسْقُطُ دَيْنَ النَّفَقَةِ بِهَلَا ِك فِي يَدِ الْمُلْتَقِطِ قَبْلَ الْحَبْسِ وَيَسْقُطُ إِذَا هَلَكَ بَعْدَ الْحَبْسِ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ بِالْحَبْسِ شَبيه الرهن

ترجمہ پھر اگر قاضی کے حکم کے بعد مالک آ گیا تو اس ملتقط کو یہ اختیار ہو گا کہ جانور اس کے حوالہ کرنے سے انکار کر دے یہاں تک کہ وہ پچھلا تمام خرچ لا کر اسی ملقط کو دے دے۔ کیونکہ اس کے خرچ کرنے سے جانور زندہ رہا ہے۔ تو دوسرے لفظوں میں یوں کہا جائے گا کہ گویا یہ ملتقط کی اجازت سے اس جانور کا مالک ہو گیا ہے۔ اور اب وہ جانور گویا اس کے ہاتھوں فروخت ہو گیا ہے ) ۔ یعنی جتنا اس نے خرچ کیا ہے اسی انداز سے یہ جانور اس ملتقط کے پاس بک گیا ہے۔ اور اسی صورت کے قریب تر وہ شخص بھی ہے جو کسی کے بھاگے ہوئے غلام کو پکڑ کر لے آیا ۔ کیونکہ اسے بھی اختیار ہے اپنا وہ خرچ اس مالک سے پہلے وصول کرلے جو اس نے اس کی حفاظت میں کیا ہے۔ اس کے بعد ہی یہ غلام اس کے حوالہ کرے۔ اس کی وجہ بھی وہی ہے جو ابھی بیان کی گئی ہے۔ پھر اگر جانور کو روک لینے اور مالک کے حوالہ کرنے سے انکار سے پہلے اس ملتقط کے قبضہ میں جانور ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس کے خرچ کے سلسلہ کا قرض ختم نہیں ہوگا ۔ البتہ اگر روکنے کے بعد جانور ہلاک ہوا تو وہ قرض بھی ختم ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ جانور کے روکنے کی وجہ سے اب یہ مسئلہ رہن کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اور رہن رکھا ہوا مال جس کے پاس رکھا ہوا ہوتا ہے اگر اس کے پاس ہلاک ہو جاتا ہے تو وہ قرضہ کے بدلہ ختم ہو جاتا ہے)۔
He said: Then when the owner appears, the finder has the right to detain it from him until he brings the nafaqah, because he (the finder) gave life to it with his nafaqah, so it is as if he acquired ownership from his side. So it is like a sale. And closer to this is the return of a runaway slave, for he has the right to detain him for the collection of the reward (ju'l) for what we mentioned. Then the debt of nafaqah is not extinguished by its destruction in the hand of the finder before detention, and it is extinguished if it is destroyed after detention, because it becomes by detention similar to a rahn (pawn).

Translation: Then if after the judge's order the owner comes, the finder will have the right to refuse to hand over the animal until he brings all previous expenses and gives them to the finder. Because the animal lived due to his expense. So in other words, it is as if the finder became owner of this animal by his permission. And now the animal is as if sold by his hand. That is, in the same amount he spent, this animal is sold to the finder. And closer to this scenario is the person who catches someone's runaway slave. Because he also has the right to first recover his expenses that he incurred for his protection before handing over the slave. The reason is the same as stated above. Then if the animal perishes in the possession of the finder before detaining and refusing to hand over, the debt of his expense is not extinguished. However, if the animal perishes after detention, then that debt is also extinguished. Because due to the locking, this matter has become similar to a pawn. And a pawned property, if it perishes with the person with whom it is pawned, then it extinguishes the debt in exchange.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Hidayah (with commentary) gives the ruling when the owner of the found animal appears after the judge has ordered nafaqah. The finder has the right to detain the animal until the owner pays all the nafaqah expenses. The reasoning is that the finder's expenditure preserved the animal's life, so it is as if the finder acquired ownership of the animal from the owner's side (like a sale). The analogy is made to the case of returning a runaway slave (radd al-abiq), where the finder can also detain the slave until paid. Further, if the animal is destroyed before detention, the debt of nafaqah is not extinguished, but if it is destroyed after detention, it is extinguished because the detention makes the animal like a rahn (pawn), and destruction of a pawn extinguishes the debt.

Key Terms
حَبْس (habs): Detention of the animal by the finder until payment.
رہن (rahn): A contract of pledge where property is held as security for a debt.
راد الآبق (radd al-abiq): Return of a runaway slave to the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a finder detains a found animal and it dies before the owner pays nafaqah, what happens to the debt?
A) Debt remains
B) Debt is extinguished
C) Debt is halved
D) Finder must compensate the owner

Key Takeaway
The finder of a lost animal may detain it until the owner reimburses expenses; this right is analogized to the case of a runaway slave, and valid detention makes possession akin to a pawn.

Ruling on Luqata in Hal and Haram: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute with Shafi'i over whether luqata in Haram requires indefinite announcing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on luqata in the Haram, explain the Shafi'i counterargument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Luqata in the Haram: same as outside — announce for one year, then give in charity.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic ikhtilaf between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the obligation of announcing a found object (luqata) in the sacred precinct of Mecca. At stake is whether the sanctity of the Haram changes the duration of announcement or whether it remains identical to luqata elsewhere.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
According to Quduri, luqata in Hal and Haram are equal: the finder announces for one year, then may give in charity.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that announcing must continue until the owner appears.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i cites the hadith: 'La yahillu luqtatuha illa limunshidiha' (Its luqata is only permissible for one who announces it).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that the hadith is general; the mention of Haram emphasizes that announcing does not drop there, not that duration extends. The general hadith of 'arrafaha sanatan' applies everywhere.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Shafi'i, the finder can never own the luqata in Haram; under Hanafi, after one year the finder can give in charity and effectively own it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلُقْطَة الحِلَّ وَالْحَرَمِ سَوَاء وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَجِبُ التَّعْرِيفُ فِى لُقْطَةِ الْحَرَمِ إِلَى أَنْ يَجِيَّ صَاحِبُهَا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِى الْحَرَمِ وَلَا يَحِلُّ لُقْطَتُهَا إِلَّا لِمُنْشِدِهَا وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أُعْرِفُ عَفَاصَهَا وَوَكَائِهَا ثُمَّ عَرَفَهَا سَنَةً مِنْ غَيْرِ فَضْلٍ وَلا نَّهَا لُقْطَةً وَفِى التَّصَدِّقِ بَعْدَ مُدَّةِ التَّعْرِيفِ إِبْقَاءُ مِلْكِ الْمَالِكِ مِنْ وَجْةٍ فَيَمْلِكُهُ كَمَا فِي سَائِرِ هَلَتَأْوِيلُ مَارَوَى أَنَّهُ لَا يَحِلُّ الْإِلْتِقَاطُ الأَلِلتَّعْرِيفِ وَالتَّحْصِيصُ بِالْحَرَمِ لِبَيَانِ أَنَّهُ لَا يَسْقُطُ التَّعْرِيفُ فِيْهِ المَكَانِ أَنَّهُ لِلْغُرَبَاءِ ظَاهِرًا

ترجمہ قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ حرم مکہ اور اس کے با ہر حل دونوں جگہوں کا لقطہ برابر ہے۔ اور امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حرم کے لفظہ کا اعلان کرانا یہاں تک واجب ہے کہ اس کا مالک آجائے ۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ نے حرم کے بارے میں فرمایا ہے کہ اس کا لقط صرف اس شخص کے لئے حلال ہے جو اس کا اعلان کرائے ۔ ( بخاری اور مسلم دونوں نے اس کی روایت کی ہے )
He said: Luqata of Hal and Haram are equal. Al-Shafi'i said: In luqata of Haram, announcing is obligatory until its owner comes, because of his statement عليه السلام in the Haram: 'And its luqata is not permissible except for one who announces it.' Our proof is his statement عليه السلام: 'Identify its container and its string, then announce it for a year, without differentiation, that it is a luqata.' And in giving in charity after the period of announcing, there is preservation of the owner's ownership from one aspect, so he owns it as in other [cases]. The interpretation of what he narrated that picking up is not permissible except for announcing, and the specification of Haram is to show that announcing does not fall in it, because the place is for strangers apparently.

Translation: Quduri (may Allah have mercy on him) said that the luqata of the Haram of Mecca and outside it (Hal) are equal. And Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said that in the Haram, announcing the found object is obligatory until its owner comes, because the Messenger of Allah said regarding the Haram: 'Its found object is only permissible for the one who announces it.' (Both Bukhari and Muslim narrated it).
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents the dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the ruling of luqata in the Haram (sanctuary of Mecca). The Hanafi position, stated by Quduri, is that luqata in Hal and Haram are the same: the finder announces for one year and then may give in charity or use. Shafi'i holds that in the Haram, announcing must continue until the owner appears, based on a hadith that luqata in Haram is only permissible for one who announces it (implying indefinite announcement). The Hanafi response is that the general hadith of 'Identify its container and string, then announce for a year' applies equally to all places, and the specification of the Haram in the other hadith is to emphasize that announcing is not dropped in the Haram, not that it should be indefinite. The Hanafis interpret the Shafi'i proof as a general ruling for all luqata, with the mention of Haram indicating that the obligation of announcing is not waived there.

Key Terms
حل (hal): Outside the Haram (sanctuary) of Mecca.
حرم (haram): The sacred precinct of Mecca.
منشد (munshid): One who announces a lost item publicly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for luqata found in the Haram of Mecca?
A) It must be announced indefinitely until the owner appears.
B) It is the same as luqata outside: announce for one year then give in charity.
C) It cannot be picked up at all.
D) It becomes the property of the finder immediately.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that luqata in the Haram and outside are equal; announcing is wajib for one year, after which the finder may give in charity.

Luqata in the Haram: Same Rules Apply
Inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafi vs Shafi‘i on luqata in Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on luqata in the Haram and explain how the Hanafi school harmonizes the two hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Luqata in the Haram is not exempt from announcement; the obligation applies everywhere.

When you find a lost item in the sacred precinct of Makkah, does the ruling change? Imam al-Shafi‘i thought it might, citing a special hadith. The Hanafi school, however, maintains consistency: the obligation to announce luqata for one year applies regardless of location. In this lesson, we unpack the proofs and reasoning behind this Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on luqata in the Haram
Begin by identifying what the Hanafi school says about picking up and announcing luqata in the Haram. Note that it is permissible to pick up with the intention to announce, and announcement is obligatory (wajib) for one year.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi‘i held that luqata in the Haram can only be picked up by one who announces, implying a stricter rule or even prohibition without immediate announcement.
The key hadith for Shafi‘i is 'لاَ تُلْتَقَطْ لُقَطَتُهُ إِلاَّ لِمُنْشِدٍ'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from the general command
The Hanafi school relies on the general hadith from the Six Books: 'اعْرِفْ عِفَاصَهَا وَوِكَاءَهَا ثُمَّ عَرِّفْهَا سَنَةً'. This command makes no distinction between Halal and Haram, indicating it applies universally.
The imperative 'عَرِّفْ' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
4
Examine the Hanafi interpretation of the Shafi‘i proof
The hadith cited by Shafi‘i (Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim) is understood not as a prohibition, but as an emphasis that announcement is obligatory even in the Haram. The specification of Haram is to remove the misconception that announcement might be waived due to the large number of travelers.
The Hanafi response harmonizes the two hadith by treating the first as general and the second as affirming the obligation in a specific context.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Identify the difference in legal application: According to Hanafi, a person may pick up luqata in the Haram and announce it; according to Shafi‘i, it is not permissible to pick up without the intention to announce, and some views even forbid picking up altogether.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and relied upon in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ نے لقطہ پانے والے کو فرمایا ہے کہ تم اس کے ظرف اور اس کی بندھن کو محفوظ کر لو اور ایک سال تک اس کا اعلان کرو صحاح ستہ نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ حالانکہ اس حکم میں حل ہونے یا حرم ہونے کی کوئی تفصیل بیان نہیں فرمائی ہے ۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ حرم کا لقطہ بھی ایک لقطہ ہی ہوتا ہے اور اعلان کی مدت کے بعد صدقہ کرنے میں ایک طرح کی ملکیت اس کے مالک کے لئے باقی رکھنی ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے دوسرے لقطوں کی طرح اس میں بھی مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے جو حدیث روایت کی ہے اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اس کا لقطہ اٹھا لینا صرف اس کے لئے حلال ہے جو اس کے بارے میں اعلان کرادے ۔ پھر حرم کو خاص کر اس بات کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے بیان کیا گیا ہے کہ حرم کے لقطہ میں بھی اعلان کر انا معاف نہیں ہوگا ۔ بلکہ اس کا اعلان بھی ضروری ہے۔ اس وہم کو دور کرنے کے لئے ہے کہ یہ تو بے شمار مسافروں کی جگہ ہے۔ (یعنی یہاں حج کرنے کے لئے دور دور سے بہت زیادہ تعداد میں لوگ آتے ہیں تو ظاہر ہے مال کسی مسافر ہی کا ہوگا۔ ایسی صورت میں اس طرح پکارنے اور اعلان کرانے میں کوئی فائدہ بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کا مالک اب لوٹ کر آنے والا نہیں ہے۔ پس رسول اللہ نے اس طرح کا عام حکم فرما کر اس وہم کو دور کر دیا اور اس کا اعلان واجب رکھا۔ اور ظاہر حدیث کا پس منظر یا پہلے سے تعلق یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ نے فتح مکہ کے دن بلند آواز سے خطبہ دیتے ہوئے فرمایا۔ جس میں یہ فرمایا ہے کہ یہ شہر وہی ہے جس کو اللہ تعالیٰ عزوجل نے آسمان وزمین کی پیدائش کے دن ہی محترم کر دیا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے محترم کر دینے سے قیامت تک کے لئے محترم ہے۔ اس کے کانٹے نہ کاٹے جائیں ۔ اور اس کا شکار بھی نہ کیا جائے ۔ اور اس کا لقط صرف وہی اٹھائے جو اس کی تشہیر کرائے ۔ ( رواه البخاری و مسلم )
Our proof is that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said to the finder of luqata: 'Preserve its container and its tie, and announce it for one year.' The six authentic books narrated it. Yet in this command, no detail about whether it is Halal or Haram is mentioned. And also from this proof: that the luqata of the Haram is also a luqata, and after the period of announcement, when giving it in charity, a kind of ownership remains for its owner. Therefore, like other luqata, he will become the owner. As for the hadith narrated by Imam al-Shafi‘i, its meaning is that picking up its luqata is only halal for one who makes an announcement about it. Then the specification of the Haram was mentioned to make clear that in the luqata of the Haram, announcement is not excused; rather, its announcement is obligatory. It is to remove the misunderstanding that this is a place of countless travelers (that is, many people come from far and wide for Hajj, so the property apparently belongs to some traveler; in such a case, calling out and announcing would be useless, because its owner will not return). So the Messenger of Allah ﷺ issued such a general command and removed this misunderstanding, and made its announcement obligatory. The background of the apparent hadith or its connection to the previous is that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ gave a sermon in a loud voice on the day of the conquest of Makkah, in which he said: 'This city is the one which Allah Almighty declared sacred on the day He created the heavens and the earth. Therefore, by Allah's declaration of sanctity, it is sacred until the Day of Judgment. Its thorns shall not be cut, its game shall not be hunted, and its luqata shall only be picked up by one who announces it.' (Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim)
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi‘i (may Allah have mercy on him) regarding the ruling on luqata (lost property) found in the Haram of Makkah. The Hanafi position is that luqata in the Haram is treated identically to luqata outside the Haram: the finder must preserve it, announce it for one year, and after that may either keep it or give it in charity, with ownership remaining for the original owner should he appear. The proof is the general hadith from the Sahih Sittah where the Prophet ﷺ commanded announcing luqata for a year without distinguishing between Hal and Haram. The Hanafis add that the property in the Haram is also luqata, so it falls under the same ruling. Imam al-Shafi‘i relied on the hadith narrated in Bukhari and Muslim that in the Haram, 'its luqata is only picked up by one who announces it.' The Hanafis interpret this hadith not as prohibiting picking up, but as emphasizing that announcement is obligatory even in the Haram, contrary to a possible misconception that because the Haram is frequented by travelers and the owner is unlikely to return, announcement could be waived. The Prophet’s general command in the other hadith and his specific mention of announcement in the Haram together confirm that announcement is required in both cases. Thus, the Hanafi school affirms that picking up luqata in the Haram is permissible with the intention to announce, and the obligation of announcement stands.

Key Terms
لقطة (luqata): Lost property found by someone other than its owner.
حرم (haram): The sacred precinct of Makkah.
اعلان / تشہیر (i‘lan / tashhir): Public announcement of found property to locate its owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on picking up luqata in the Haram of Makkah?
A) It is absolutely prohibited.
B) It is permissible only if the finder intends to announce it for a year.
C) It is permissible without any announcement because the owner will not return.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Luqata in the Haram is governed by the same rules as all other luqata: announcement for one year is wajib, and picking up is permissible with that intention.

Witnesses vs Description for Luqata Claim
Hanafi view that claimant must produce witnesses; Maliki/Shafi‘i consider description sufficient

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires witnesses for a luqata claimant and distinguish the practical consequence from the Maliki/Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Possession (yad) is a substantive right like ownership; thus witnesses are required, not mere description.

You find a lost wallet. Someone comes and describes it perfectly. Do you have to give it to them? In the Hanafi school, you may, but you are not compelled—unless they bring witnesses. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this rule and why other schools disagree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The dispute is about what proof a claimant of luqata (found property) must provide to compel the finder to return it. The Hanafi school says witnesses; the Maliki/Shafi'i schools say description is enough.
The issue hinges on whether possession (yad) is considered a substantive right like ownership.
2
State the Hanafi Position
The finder is not compelled to return the luqata unless the claimant produces witnesses (bayyinah). A mere correct description makes return permissible but not obligatory.
The finder may voluntarily return upon description, but the judge cannot force him.
3
State the Opposing School's View
Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that if the claimant gives an accurate description (weight, number, container, knot), the finder must return the item, and the judge compels it.
They argue that the dispute is over possession, not ownership, so description alone resolves it.
4
Analyze Each Side's Legal Proof (Dalil)
Hanafi: possession is analogous to ownership (qiyas), so the claimant needs proof—witnesses. They cite the hadith 'al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i'. The opposing schools cite the hadith 'fa in jaa sahibuha...' which commands return upon recognition. Hanafi interprets this command as permissibility (ibahah), not obligation.
The Hanafi response reconciles the two hadiths by giving priority to the general principle of evidence.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Under Hanafi law, a claimant with correct description but no witnesses cannot force return; the finder may keep the item (though recommended to return). Under Maliki/Shafi'i, the judge orders return based on description alone.
This difference affects the finder's liability and the owner's ability to reclaim property.

وَإِذَا حَضَرَ رَجُلْ فَادَّعى اللُّقْطَة لَمْ تُدْفَعْ إِلَيْهِ حَتَّى يُقِيمَ الْبَيِّنَةَ فَإِنْ أَعْطى عَلَامَتُهَا حَلَّ لِلْمُلْتَقِطِ أَنْ يَدْفَعَهَا إِلَيْهِ وَ لا يُجْبَرُ عَلى ذَالِكَ فِى الْفَضَلِهِ وَ قَالَ مَالِك وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يُجْبَرُ وَ الْعَلَامَةُ مِثْل أَنْ يُسَمَّى وَزُنَ الدَّرَاهِم وَعَدَدِهَا وَوِكَائِهَا وَوِعَائِهَا لَهُمَا أَنَّ صَاحِبَ الْيَدِينَازِعُهُ فِي الْيَدِوَلَا يُنَازِعُهُ فِى الْمِلْكِ فَيُشْتَرَطُ الوَصْفُ لِوُجُودِ الْمُنَازَعَةِ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَلَا تُشْتَرِطُ إِقَامَةُ الْبَيِّنَةِ لِعَدَمِ الْمُسَارَعَةِ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْيَدَحَقٌّ مَقْصُودُ كَالْمِلْكِ فَلا يَسْتَحِقَّ إِلا لِحُجَّةِ وَهُوَ الْبَيِّنَةُ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْمِلْكِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ تَحِلُّ لَهُ الدَّفَعُ عِنْدَ إِصَابَةِ الْعَلَامَةِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَإِنْ جَاءَ صَاحِبُهَا وَعَرِفَ عِفَاصَهَا وَعَدَدَهَا فَادْفَعْهَا إِلَيْهِ وَهُدَ الْإِبَاحَةِ عَمَلًا بِالْمَشْهُورِ وَهُوَ قُولُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ البينَةُ عَلَى الْمُدَّعَى الْحَدِيث
ترجمہ: اور جب کسی شخص نے (حاکم کے پاس حاضر ہو کر لقطہ کا دعوی کیا – کہ وہ مال لقطہ میرا ہی ہے) تو جب تک اس پر وہ گواہ پیش نہ کر دے اسے وہ نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اس کے بعد اگر اس نے کوئی علامت بیان کی تو اسے دینے پر مجبور کرے گا) اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح مالک ہونا ایک حق مقصود ہے اسی طرح قبضہ کا ہونا بھی ایک حق مقصود ہے۔ اس لئے مطالبہ کرنے والا بغیر دلیل کے اس کا مستحق نہ ہوگا اور یہاں پر دلیل گواہی کو پیش کرنا ہے۔ ملکیت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے (اسی لئے بغیر گواہ پیش کئے ہوئے دینے پر پانے والے مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا)۔ ہاں اسی صورت میں مجبور کیا جائے گا کہ وہ اس سامان کی علامتیں بالکل صحیح بیان کر دے تو اس وقت اس ملتقط کو مال مالک کے حوالہ کر دینا جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر اس کا مالک آجائے اور اس مال کے بارے میں یہ بتادے کہ وہ کیسی چیز یا کیسے تھیلہ میں تھا اور اس کی تعداد کتنی تھی تو وہ مال اس کے حوالہ کر دے ۔ اسلم، ابوداؤد اور نسائی نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ مالک کو دینے کا یہ حکم اباحت کے طور پر ہے۔ یعنی اسے دینا مباح ہے اور لازم نہیں ہے)۔ تا کہ حدیث مشہور پر عمل باقی رہے اور حدیث مشہور سے وہ حدیث مراد ہے جس میں فرمایا ہے کہ مدعی پر گواہ پیش کرنا لازم ہے ۔ اور منکر پر قسم کھانا ہے۔ (حاصل کلام یہ ہوا کہ اگر مالک نے گواہ پیش کئے تو قاضی بھی اسے دینے کا حکم کرے گا۔ اور اگر صرف اس کی صحیح علامتیں بتادے تو اسے اختیار ہے کہ چاہے دے یا نہ دے)
تشریح: اگر کسی نے لقطہ کا دعویٰ کیا کہ یہ میری ملکیت ہے تو ملتقط اس کے حوالے نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ گواہ قائم کرے یا اگر مدعی نے صحیح طور پر علامات بتا دیں تو لقطہ مدعی کے حوالے کرنا جائز ہے۔ لیکن قاضی ملتقط کو مجبور نہیں کر سکتا کہ لقطہ حوالے کر دے۔ اسلئے کہ قبضہ بھی ملکیت کی طرح مقصود ہے اور مدعی بغیر دلیل کے ملتقط کا حقدار نہیں جبکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حدیث ہے جو شخص عین مال پائے وہی اس کا زیادہ حق دار ہے لہذا دوسرے شخص کو دلیل و حجت کے بعد لقطہ حوالے کیا جائے گا اور وہ گواہ قائم کرنا ہے اور یہ وہی دلیل ہے اور اگر گواہ نہ ہوں تو کم از کم علامات بتا دے جیسے حدیث میں آیا ہے،
فَإِنْ جَاءَ صَاحِبُهَا وَ عَرَفَ عِفَاصَهَا وَعَدَدَهَا فَادْفَعُهَا إِلَيْهِ
اور علامات بیان کرنے کے بعد یہ بھی ملتقط کو اختیار ہے کہ لقطہ مدعی کے حوالے نہ کرے۔ اسلئے کہ علامات کا بیان کرنا شہادت سے کم درجہ ہے۔
امام مالک و شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ تنازع قبضہ میں ہے نہ کہ لقطہ کی ملکیت میں اس لئے علامات بیان کرنے سے لقطہ مدعی کے حوالے کرنا پڑے گا گواہ قائم کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں حتی کہ قاضی ملتقط کو مجبور بھی کر سکتا ہے کہ وہ لقطہ مدعی کے حوالے کرے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا قبضہ ملکیت کی طرح حق مقصود ہے اور بلا دلیل مدعی حقدار نہیں اور دلیل گواہ ہیں حدیث میں ہے الْبَيِّنَةُ عَلَى المُرَّع .... الخ اور امام شافعی کی مستدل حدیث فَإِنْ جَاءَ صَاحِبُهَا وَعَرَفَ ... الخ بيان جواز پر محمول ہے یعنی حوالے کرنا جائز ہے لازم نہیں ۔
When a man claims the luqata, it is not given to him until he produces evidence (bayyinah). If he gives its description, it becomes permissible for the finder to hand it over to him, but he is not compelled to do so in the opinion of Abu Hanifah. Malik and al-Shafi‘i said: He is compelled. The description is like specifying the weight, number, tie, and bag of the dirhams. Their argument: The finder disputes with the owner about possession (yad), not about ownership (milk). So description is required because there is a dispute from one perspective, but establishing evidence is not required because there is no dispute from another perspective. Our argument: Possession is a substantive right like ownership, so the claimant does not deserve it without proof, and that proof is evidence (bayyinah), analogized to ownership. However, it is permissible for the finder to hand it over when the description matches, due to the Prophet’s saying: 'If its owner comes and recognizes its container and its number, then give it to him.' This indicates permissibility (ibahah), acting upon the well-known hadith, which is his saying: 'Evidence is upon the claimant.' Translation: And when a person (appears before the judge and claims the luqata, that it is his property), it will not be given to him until he produces witnesses. If he mentions a description, the finder may hand it over, but the judge will not compel him. Imam Malik and Shafi‘i said: He should be compelled. The description could be: if they are dirhams, their weight, number, what bag or pouch they were in, what kind of knot was tied on it, etc. Their proof is that the finder is disputing with the owner about possession, not ownership. Therefore, describing the item is sufficient because there is a dispute in one aspect; establishing witnesses is not required because there is no dispute in another aspect (i.e., the finder does not claim ownership, only possession; so witnesses are not needed; rather, the owner should identify his property and thus should be compelled to hand it over). Our proof is that just as ownership is a substantive right, possession is also a substantive right. Therefore, the claimant does not deserve it without proof, and here proof is witnesses, by analogy with ownership. Hence, the finder cannot be compelled to hand over without witnesses. Yes, he may be compelled if the description exactly matches, and then the finder may hand over the property to the owner, because the Prophet said: 'If its owner comes and tells about the item – what kind of thing or bag it was and its number – then hand over the property to him.' This is reported by Aslam, Abu Dawud, and Nasa’i. This command to hand over is on the basis of permissibility (ibahah), i.e., handing over is permissible, not obligatory, so that the well-known hadith remains operative, which states that the claimant must produce witnesses and the defendant must take an oath. (In summary, if the owner produces witnesses, the judge will order the finder to hand over; if he only gives accurate description, the finder has the option to give or not). Explanation: If someone claims the luqata as his property, the finder should not hand it over until he establishes witnesses; if the claimant correctly describes it, it is permissible for the finder to hand over, but the judge cannot compel the finder. Because possession is like ownership – a substantive right – and the claimant is not entitled to it without proof, based on the Prophet’s hadith: 'Whoever finds an item, he has more right to it.' Therefore, another person gets the luqata only after proof and evidence, which is establishing witnesses. And if there are no witnesses, at least he should give description, as in the hadith: 'If its owner comes and recognizes its container and its number, then give it to him.' After describing, the finder also has the option not to hand over, because description is a lower degree than testimony. Imam Malik and Shafi‘i say: The dispute is about possession, not ownership, so description is sufficient and the finder must hand over; even the judge can compel him. Imam Abu Hanifah said: Possession is a substantive right like ownership, and the claimant is not entitled without proof, and proof is witnesses. The hadith used by Shafi‘i (Fa in jaa sahibuha…) is interpreted as permissibility, not obligation.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the procedure when a person claims a found object (luqata). The core issue: what proof must the claimant provide to have the luqata handed over? The Hanafi school (Imam Abu Hanifah) holds that the claimant must produce witnesses (bayyinah) to prove ownership. Only then is the finder compelled to return it. If the claimant merely describes the item correctly (e.g., weight, number, bag, knot), the finder may voluntarily hand it over, but the judge cannot compel him. The Maliki and Shafi‘i schools argue that since the dispute is over possession (yad) and not ownership (milk), description is sufficient and the finder should be compelled. Their analogy: the finder claims possession, not ownership, so the owner’s identification of his property resolves the dispute without formal witnesses. The Hanafi response: possession is a substantive right just like ownership; therefore, the claimant must provide proof, which in legal terms is witnesses. The hadith 'If its owner comes and recognizes its container and its number, then give it to him' is interpreted as giving permission (ibahah) to hand over, not a command (wujub). This harmonizes it with the well-known principle 'al-bayyinatu ‘ala al-mudda‘i' (the burden of proof is on the claimant). The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, a claimant who describes the luqata correctly but has no witnesses cannot force the finder to return it; the finder may keep it (though it is recommended to return). Under Maliki/Shafi‘i, the judge would order return on description alone.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically two male witnesses or one man and two women in financial matters.
علامت / وصف (‘alamah / wasf): Description of the found item (e.g., weight, number, container, knot).
ملتقط (multaqit): The person who picks up the luqata (finder).
عفاص (‘ifas): The container (bag, pouch) in which the item is kept.
وکاء (wika’): The tie or string used to close the container.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a claimant accurately describes the luqata (e.g., weight, bag, knot) but has no witnesses, can the judge compel the finder to return it?
A) Yes, because description proves ownership.
B) No, because possession is a substantive right like ownership, requiring witnesses.
C) Yes, because the dispute is only about possession.
D) No, because the finder has absolute ownership after one year.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires witnesses to compel return of luqata; description alone only permits voluntary return because possession is a substantive right.

Reward for Returning a Runaway Slave: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Dispute on obligatory reward for returning a runaway

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the reward (ju‘l) for returning a runaway slave and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school obligates forty dirhams for returning a runaway from three days' travel, based on sahaba consensus and istihsan—not strict qiyas.

In this lesson, we examine a classic inter-madhhab dispute on whether a reward is due for returning a runaway slave without prior agreement. The Hanafi school, using istihsan, rules it obligatory; the Shafi'i school, following qiyas, denies it. The passage from al-Quduri sets out the Hanafi position and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the ju‘l
Identify the exact ruling: forty dirhams for a three-day journey, proportional for less. The reward is wajib upon the master, not voluntary.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the Shafi'i opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that no reward is due unless stipulated by contract, based on qiyas to the stray slave.
The qiyas treats the returner as a volunteer (mutatawwi‘).
3
Examine the Hanafi proof from sahaba consensus
The Companions agreed on the principle of obligation (wujūb aṣl al-ju‘l); they only differed on the amount. The Hanafis reconciled by setting forty for full travel distance.
This consensus is cited as ‘anfaqū ‘alā wujūb aṣl al-ju‘l.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal of qiyas
The stray does not hide, while the runaway hides; thus the need for safeguarding is greater. Also, the amount is determined by transmission (sam‘) from the sahaba, not by analogy.
The difference in ‘illa (effective cause) breaks the qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a Hanafi master must pay forty dirhams if the slave is returned from three days' distance; under Shafi'i, no payment unless a condition was made.
This shows the practical impact of the methodological difference.

قَالَ وَ مَنْ رَدَّ آبقًا عَلَى مَوْلَاهُ مِنْ مَسيرَةِ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فَصَاعِدًا فَلَهُ عَلَيْهِ جَعَلَهُ أَرْبَعُونَ دِرْهَمًا وَإِنْ رَدَّهُ لِأَقَلِّ مِنْ ذَلِكَ فَبِحِسَابِهِ وَهَذَا اسْتِحْسَانٌ وَالْقِيَاسُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ لَهُ شَيْءٌ إِلَّا بِالشَّرْطِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ لِأَنَّهُ مُتَطَوِّعٌ بِمَنَافِعِهِ فَأَشْبَهَ الْعَبْدَ الضَّالَّ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ رِضْوَانُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِمْ أَنْفَقُوا عَلَى وُجُوبِ أَصْلِ الْجُعَلِ إِلَّا أَنَّ مِنْهُمْ مَنْ أَوْجَبَ أَرْبَعِينَ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ أَوْجَبَ مَادُونَهَا فَأَوْجَبْنَا الْأَرْبَعِينَ فِي مَسِيرَةِ السَّفَرِ وَمَا دُونَهَا فِيمَا دُونَهُ تَوْفِيقًا وَتَلْفِيقًا بَيْنَهُمَا وَلِأَنَّ إِيجَابَ الْجُعَلِ أَصْلُهُ حَامِلٌ عَلَى الرَّدِّ إِذِ الْحَسْبَةُ نَادِرَةً فَتَحْصُلُ صِيَانَةَ أَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ وَالتَّقْدِيرُ بِالسَّمْعِ وَلَا سَمْعَ فِي الضَّالِّ فَامْتَنَعَ وَلِأَنَّ الْحَاجَةَ إِلَى صِيَانَةِ الضَّالِّ دُونَهَا إِلَى صِيَانَةِ الْأَبِقِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَتَوَارَى وَالْآبِقُ يَخْتَفِي وَيُقَدَّرُ الرَّضْحُ فِي الرَّدِّ عَمَّا دُونَ السَّفَرِ بِاصْطِلَاحِهِمَا أَوْ يُقَوَّضُ إِلَى رَأْيِ الْقَاضِي وَقِيلَ يُقَسَّمُ الْأَرْبَعُونَ عَلَى الْأَيَّامِ الثَّلَاثَةِ إِذْ هِيَ أَقَلُّ مُدَّةِ السَّفَرِ
He said: Whoever returns a runaway slave to his master from a distance of three days' journey or more, then upon the master is a reward of forty dirhams; and if he returns him from less than that, then proportional. This is istihsan. The qiyas is that he would have nothing unless by condition; that is the saying of al-Shafi'i, because the returner is volunteering his services, so it resembles the stray slave. Our proof: The Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) agreed on the obligation of the principle of the reward, except that some of them obligated forty and some obligated less than that; so we obligated forty for the distance of travel and less than that for what is shorter, reconciling between them. Also, making the reward obligatory is an incentive for return because seeking reward is rare, so people's wealth is preserved. The determination of the amount is by revelation, and there is no revelation concerning the stray, so it is prevented. Also, the need to safeguard the stray is less than the need to safeguard the runaway because the stray does not hide, while the runaway hides. For the reward in returning from less than travel distance, it is determined by their mutual agreement or referred to the judge's opinion. It is also said that the forty dirhams are divided over the three days, as it is the minimum duration of travel.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the reward (ju‘l) for returning a runaway slave. The matn (Quduri) states: Whoever returns a runaway from a distance of three days' travel or more is entitled to forty dirhams from the master; for less, a proportional amount. This is declared as istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas (analogy) would give nothing unless stipulated, which is Imam al-Shafi'i's position—since the returner volunteers his service, it resembles the stray slave where no reward is due. The Hanafi response (lana) provides multiple proofs: 1) The Companions agreed on the principle of reward but differed on the amount; the Hanafis reconciled by setting forty for travel distance and proportional for less. 2) Making ju‘l obligatory encourages return, as few act solely for divine reward; thus people's wealth is safeguarded. 3) The specific amount (forty) is determined by transmission (sam‘)—narrations from Companions like ‘Ammār ibn Yāsir setting ten dirhams for within the city and forty for outside. 4) The need for safeguarding a runaway is greater than for a stray because a runaway hides. For distances less than travel, the amount is set by mutual agreement or left to the judge's discretion. Some said the forty are divided over the three days. This passage shows how Hanafi fiqh uses istihsan and sahaba practice over strict qiyas.

Key Terms
جعل (ju‘l): A fixed reward (forty dirhams) given to the returner of a runaway slave from a distance of three days' travel.
رضح (radh): A lesser compensation given for returning a runaway from a distance shorter than travel distance, determined by mutual consent or judge.
استحسان (istiḥsān): A method of juristic preference that sets aside strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling, based on stronger evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for obligating a reward (ju‘l) for returning a runaway slave without prior stipulation?
A) A direct Quranic verse commanding payment.
B) Consensus (ijma) of the Companions on the principle of reward.
C) Analogy (qiyas) to the reward for finding lost property.
D) The argument that the returner is a hired worker.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates a reward for returning a runaway slave based on sahaba consensus and istihsan, even without prior stipulation, unlike the Shafi'i position that requires a contract.

The Reward for Returning a Runaway Slave: Hanafi Position and Proof
Explains the reward for returning a runaway slave based on distance, with proof from Sahaba consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the reward for returning a runaway slave, explain the proof from Sahaba consensus, and distinguish it from the case of a stray slave.

Core Idea
A reward is due for a runaway; amount depends on distance, based on Sahaba consensus.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the reward (ju'l) for returning a runaway slave. The Hanafis hold that a fixed reward of forty dirhams is owed when the slave is returned from a travel distance (three days or more), and proportionally less for shorter distances. This position is grounded in the consensus of the Companions (ijma) and the principle of istihsan, overriding the analogy to stray slaves where no reward is due. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents this ruling and responds to the Shafi'i objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The central question: Is there a fixed reward for returning a runaway slave, and if so, how much?
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
The Hanafis rule that forty dirhams are obligatory for a full travel distance, and less for shorter distances. Their proof is the consensus of the Companions, who agreed that a reward is due, though amounts varied.
The amount is set by transmitted evidence (hadith), not by analogy.
3
Examine the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes returning a runaway to returning a stray slave, which is an act of charity with no fixed reward unless the owner promised one.
This is pure qiyas without text.
4
Understand the Hanafi response using istihsan
The Hanafis reject the analogy because a runaway hides and presents a greater risk of loss, requiring a stronger incentive. The transmitted evidence (Sahaba consensus) sets the reward for a runaway but not for a stray, so istihsan overrides qiyas.
Istihsan is used to prefer the consensus over pure analogy.
5
Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In the Hanafi school, a reward is owed by default for returning a runaway; in the Shafi'i school, no reward is due unless promised by the owner. This affects the financial obligation of the owner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَنْ أَوْجَبَ أَرْبَعِينَ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ أوْجَبَ مَادُونَهَا فَأَوْجَبْنَا الْأَرْبَعِينَ فِي مَسِيرَةِ السَّفَرِ وَمَا دُونَهَا فِيمَادُونَهُ تَوْفِيقًا وَتَلْفِيقًا بَيْنَهُمَا وَلِأَنَّ إِيجَابَ الْجُعَلِ أصْلُهُ حَامِلُ عَلَى الرَّدِّإِذِ الْحَسْبَةُ نَادِرَةً فَتَحْصِلُ صِيانَةَ أَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ وَالتَّقْدِيرُ بِالسَّمْعِ وَلَا سَمْعَ فِي الضَّالِ فَامْتَنَعَ وَلِأَنَّ الْحَاجَةَ إِلى صَيَانَةِ الضَّالِ دُونَهَا إِلى صِيَانَةِ الْأَبِقِ لأنَّه لَا يَتَوَارَى وَالْابِقُ يَخْتَفِى وَيُقَدَّرُ الرَّضْحُ فِي الرَّدِ عَمَّا دُونَ السَّفَرِ بِإِصْطِلاحِهِمَا أَوْ يُقَوَّضُ إِلَى رَأَي الْقَاضِي وَقِيلَ يُقَسَّمُ الْأَرْبَعُونَ عَلَى الْأيَّامِ الثَّلَاثَةِ إِذْهِي أَقَلّ مُدَّةِ السَّفَرِ
Some made it obligatory (to give) forty, and some made it obligatory less than that. So we made forty obligatory for the distance of travel, and less than that for less than it, as a reconciliation and combination between them. And because the imposition of the reward is fundamentally a motive for return, since fulfilling the duty (of returning) is rare. Thus, protection of people's wealth is achieved. And the estimation (of amount) is by transmitted evidence, and there is no transmitted evidence for the stray slave (al-dall), so it is not possible. And because the need for protecting the stray is less than that for protecting the runaway, because it (the stray) does not go into hiding, while the runaway conceals itself. And the reward for return from less than travel distance is determined by their mutual agreement, or it is delegated to the judge's opinion. And it was said: the forty dirhams are divided over three days, as that is the minimum duration of travel.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute. The author (al-Hidayah) states the Hanafi position: for returning a runaway slave from a travel distance (three days or more), the reward is forty dirhams; for less than that, a proportionate amount. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference), not qiyas which would give nothing. The proof is a consensus of the Companions, though the exact amount differed: some said forty, some less. The Hanafis reconcile by linking the amount to the distance of travel. The Shafi'i position is that no reward is due unless specified by contract, because returning a runaway is an act of charity like returning a stray. The Hanafi response: the purpose of the reward is to encourage return and protect property, and the amount is set by transmitted evidence (hadith) for a runaway, while for a stray there is no text, so qiyas is not applicable. The reward for less than travel distance is either by mutual agreement or left to the judge's discretion. Some scholars said the forty dirhams are divided proportionally over three days, the minimum travel period. This rule is from Ashraf Ul Hadaya's commentary on al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
جُعْل (ju'l): A reward or compensation given to someone for performing a specific task, such as returning a runaway slave.
اسْتِحْسَان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows a departure from qiyas (analogy) in favor of a stronger evidence or convenience.
ضَالّ (dall): A stray slave who has lost its way, as opposed to a runaway (abiq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nothing, unless the owner promised a reward
B) Forty dirhams
C) The value of the slave
D) Ten dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates a reward for returning a runaway slave based on Sahaba consensus, with the amount linked to distance, contrasting with the Shafi'i view that no reward is due without contract.

Reward for a Slave Worth Less Than Forty Dirhams
Intra-Hanafi dispute on reward amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the reward for finding a runaway slave valued under forty dirhams, explain the reasoning behind each position, and apply the ruling on sulh for more or less than forty.

Core Idea
When a slave's value is below forty, Muhammad reduces the reward by one dirham; Abu Yusuf holds the text fixed at forty.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. The base text of al-Hidayah states the view of Imam Muhammad, then records the objection of Imam Abu Yusuf. Understanding this disagreement illuminates how Hanafi jurists balance textual authority (nass) with practical objectives (maqsid). The lesson also touches on the validity of compromise (sulh) regarding the reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested case
The case is a finder of a runaway slave whose value is less than forty dirhams. The question is: what reward should the finder receive?
This is the specific scenario where the imams differ.
2
State Muhammad's position and his reasoning
Imam Muhammad rules that the finder receives the slave's value minus one dirham. His reasoning: the purpose of the reward is to incentivize return and revive the owner's property; reducing one dirham ensures the finder gets something while preserving some benefit for the owner.
Muhammad focuses on the maqsid (objective) of the reward.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and his reasoning
Imam Abu Yusuf rules that the finder receives the full forty dirhams, regardless of the slave's lower value. His reasoning: the amount is fixed by nass (textual evidence, i.e., the hadith), so it cannot be reduced. He also notes that sulh (compromise) for more than forty is invalid, but sulh for less is permissible as a waiver by the finder.
Abu Yusuf prioritizes the apparent meaning of the nass.
4
Analyze the distinction on sulh
Abu Yusuf's reasoning implies that the fixed amount cannot be exceeded by agreement, but the finder can voluntarily accept less (sulh for less) because it is a waiver of his right. This distinction preserves the inviolability of the text while allowing flexibility.
This logic is consistent with Hanafi principles on rights of Allah vs. rights of servants.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative position)
Although the source does not give explicit tarjih, later Hanafi authorities (such as al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah) typically adopt Abu Yusuf's view as stronger because it adheres strictly to the nass. The mufta bihi is that the finder is entitled to forty dirhams, subject to the possibility of sulh for less.
The student should be aware that both views are valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ إِنْ كَانَتْ قِيْمَتُهُ أَقَلَّ مِنْ أَرْبَعِيْنَ يُقْضَى لَهُ بِقِيْمَتِهِ إِلَّا دِرْهِما قَالَ وَهَذَا قَولُ مُحَمَّدٌ وَ قَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَهُ أرْبَعُونَ دِرُهما لأَنَّ التَّقْدِيرَ بِهَا ثَبَتَ بِالنَّصِ فَلَا يُنْقَصُ عَنْهَا وَلِهَذَا لَا يَجُوزُ الصُّلْحُ عَلَى الزِّيَادَةِ بِخِلَافِ الصُّلْحُ عَلَى الأقل لأنَّهُ حَلٌّ مِنْهُ وَلِمُحَمَّد أَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ حَمْلُ الْغَيْرِ عَلَى الرَّدْ لِيُحْيِي مَالَ الْمَالِكِ فَيَنْقُصَ دِرْهُمْ لِيُسَلَّمَ لَهُ شَيْ تَحْقِيقًا لِلْفَائِدَةِ
He said: And if its (the slave's) value is less than forty, he is awarded its value except one dirham. He said: This is the statement of Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: He (the finder) has forty dirhams, because the estimation by it (forty) is established by the text, so it is not reduced below it. For this reason, compounding for more is not permissible, contrary to compounding for less, because (the latter) is a waiver from him. And for Muhammad: The objective is to motivate others to return (the slave) so that the owner's property is revived; thus he reduces one dirham so that something is given to him, realizing the benefit.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states a case: if the value of the runaway slave is less than forty dirhams, the finder is awarded the value minus one dirham. This is attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf disagrees: the finder receives the full forty dirhams because the amount (forty) is fixed by the textual evidence (hadith/nass), so it cannot be reduced. Supporting his view, Abu Yusuf argues that if the owner and finder agree on more than forty, it is not permissible (because it would exceed the text), but agreement on less is permissible as a waiver. Muhammad's reasoning: the purpose of the reward is to incentivize the return of the slave, which revives the owner's property. If the slave is worth less than forty, paying the full forty might not make sense; reducing one dirham ensures the finder gets something while still preserving the owner's property. This is a practical concession to achieve the intended benefit. The passage also implies that both views are recognized within the Hanafi school. This is from the commentary of Ashraf Ul Hadaya.

Key Terms
صُلْح (sulh): A settlement or compromise in which the finder and owner agree on an amount different from the prescribed reward.
نَصّ (nass): A clear textual evidence from the Qur'an or Sunnah that establishes a ruling without ambiguity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what does the finder of a runaway slave receive if the slave's value is less than forty dirhams?
A) The full forty dirhams
B) The value of the slave
C) The value of the slave minus one dirham
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The amount of reward for finding a runaway slave is subject to ikhtilaf: Muhammad reduces it when value is low, Abu Yusuf insists on forty based on the text.

The Reward for Returning a Runaway Slave: Hanafi Position and Shafi'i Dispute
States the Hanafi ruling on ja'alah and the Shafi'i disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ja'alah for returning a runaway slave and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Compensation for returning a runaway slave is wajib by hadith and istihsan, not merely voluntary.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi ruling on the reward (ja'alah) for returning a runaway slave. It also presents the disagreement of Imam al-Shafi'i, who likens it to a stray animal. The Hanafi school uses hadith and istihsan to establish wajib compensation, even though qiyas would suggest otherwise.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The returner is entitled to 40 dirhams if the distance is three days or more, proportionally if less. This is based on hadith and consensus of the Companions on the obligation.
The compensation is wajib on the master.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that returning a runaway slave is like returning a stray animal: no compensation unless the master stipulated a reward.
For Shafi'i, it is a voluntary good deed (tabarru').
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument is based on qiyas: just as a stray animal yields no reward without stipulation, so too a runaway slave.
They see no textual evidence for a fixed reward.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis cite hadiths specifically mentioning compensation for runaway slaves. They also employ istihsan (juristic preference) to override qiyas, because the hadiths create a special rule.
Istihsan is based on a stronger textual indication.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafi: wajib compensation even without stipulation. Shafi'i: no compensation unless stipulated. This practical difference affects actual financial liability.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الأباق
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم تشریح بھاگے ہوئے غلام کو تین دن یا تین دن سے زائد مسافت سے آقا کے پاس لانے والے کا عوض چالیس درہم ہیں۔ اور اگر کم مدت ( یعنی تین دن مسافت سے کم مدت) سے غلام کو لایا گیا تو اس حساب سے معاوضہ دیا جائے گا۔ وجوب معاوضہ پر تو سب صحابہ کرام نے کا اجماع ہے لیکن مقدار میں فرق ہے بعض کے ہاں چالیس درہم بعض کے ہاں اس سے کم ۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جب کوئی بھاگے ہوئے غلام کو لایا تو بھٹکے ہوئے غلام کی طرح اس کو کوئی معاوضہ نہ دیا جائے گا ۔ یہ تبرع اور احسان ہے ہاں اگر آقا شرط لگا دے تو عوض دیا جائے گا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے ہاں چونکہ احادیث میں معاوضہ کا تذکرہ ہے اور بھٹکے ہوئے غلام کے بارے میں عوض کا کوئی تذکر نہیں اب جب تین دن سے کم مدت مسافت سے غلام کو لایا گیا تو معاوضہ ان تین ایام پر تقسیم ہو گا۔
اگر چہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ غلام کو لانے والے کو معاوضہ نہ دیا جائے لیکن از روئے استحسان کے غلام کو لانے والے کو معاوضہ کا مستحق قرار دیا گیا
غلام کی قیمت چالیس درہم سے کم ہو تو واپس لانے والے کو کتنے دئیے جائیں گے
Book of Runaway Slaves. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, volume 7. Explanation: The one who brings a runaway slave from a distance of three days or more to his master is entitled to compensation of forty dirhams. And if the slave is brought from a lesser distance (i.e., less than three days' travel), then compensation will be given proportionally. On the obligation of compensation, all the Companions have consensus, but they differ on the amount; some say forty dirhams, some less. Imam al-Shafi'i says: When someone brings a runaway slave, he will not be given any compensation, just like a stray slave; it is a voluntary favor. However, if the master stipulates a condition, then compensation will be given. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that since compensations are mentioned in hadiths and there is no mention of compensation for a stray slave, when the slave is brought from a distance less than three days, the compensation is divided over those three days. Although analogy (qiyas) requires that the one who brings the slave should not be given compensation, but by way of istihsan, the one who brings the slave is deemed entitled to compensation. If the slave's value is less than forty dirhams, how much should be given to the one who returns him?
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from the Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah explains the ruling on the reward (ja'alah) for returning a runaway slave. The main ruling is that if someone brings a runaway slave from a distance of three days or more, he is entitled to 40 dirhams from the master. If the distance is less, compensation is calculated proportionally. There is consensus among the Companions on the obligation of compensation, but disagreement on the amount. Then the passage contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that bringing a runaway slave is like bringing a stray animal—it is a voluntary act with no compensation unless the master had previously stipulated a reward. The Hanafi position relies on hadiths that specify a reward, and on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas. The passage ends by introducing the next issue: what if the slave's value is less than 40 dirhams?

Key Terms
جعل (ja'alah): Reward or compensation given to someone for returning a runaway slave.
إباق (iba'): The act of a slave running away from his master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how much compensation is due for returning a runaway slave from a distance of three days or more?
A) Nothing, it is a favor.
B) 40 dirhams.
C) The slave's value.
D) It depends on the master's stipulation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that returning a runaway slave from a distance of three days or more entitles the returner to wajib compensation of 40 dirhams, based on hadith and istihsan, despite the Shafi'i objection.
