Ju'l for a Runaway Slave Who Committed Manslaughter
States ruling on ju'l when slave commits manslaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios for ju'l liability when a runaway slave commits manslaughter and determine who is responsible for the reward.

Core Idea
Ju'l follows benefit: the one who gains from the slave's return must pay the reward.

This lesson examines a ruling from Ashraf al-Hidayah regarding the reward (ju'l) for returning a runaway slave who has committed accidental killing. The ruling hinges on who bears the blood money and thus who benefits from the slave's return. Understanding this principle clarifies the Hanafi approach to conditional obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is returning a runaway slave; the ruling states that ju'l (reward) is obligatory (wajib) on someone.
The obligation is financial.
2
Recognize the two scenarios based on blood money liability
If the master pays the diyah, the reward is on the master. If the master surrenders the slave as diyah, the reward is on the heirs.
The slave's status (remaining property or transferred) changes who benefits.
3
Determine the underlying principle
The party that reaps the benefit of the slave's return must bear the expense of the reward.
Benefit is the decisive factor.
4
Apply the principle to hypothetical cases
If the master partially pays, or if the heirs refuse the slave, the principle guides the ruling.
The passage does not cover all variations, but the principle extends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الأباق
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم ترجمہ اور اگر غلام سے خطا کوئی قتل ہو گیا ہوتو دیکھا جائے گا کہ اگر اس کے مولیٰ نے اس کے قتل کا فدیہ دینا قبول کر لیا ہو تو اس غلام کو واپس لانے کا جعل اسی مولی پر لازم ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اس غلام کی واپسی سے غلام کا نفع اسی مولی کا ہوگا۔ اور اگر مولی نے قتل کے فدیہ میں یہ غلام ہی مقتول کے ورثہ کو دے دینے کا فیصلہ کر لیا ہو تو اب اس کی واپسی کا جعل بھی ان ورثہ پر ہی لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ موجودہ صورت میں اس غلام کی واپسی سے ان ورثہ ہی کو فائدہ پہنچے گا۔
Chapter of Runaway Slaves. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume seven. Commentary: And if a slave commits a mistaken killing, then it will be considered: if his master accepts to pay the blood money for the killing, then the reward for returning this slave is obligatory upon that master, because the benefit of the return of this slave goes to that master. And if the master decides to give this slave himself to the heirs of the slain as blood money, then the reward for his return becomes obligatory upon those heirs, because in this situation the benefit of the return of this slave goes to those heirs.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement (hukm) from Ashraf al-Hidayah, the Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, dealing with the reward (ju'l) for returning a runaway slave (abaq). The scenario involves a slave who has committed manslaughter (qatl al-khata'). Two sub-cases are distinguished based on how the master (mawla) handles the liability for blood money (diyah). First, if the master accepts responsibility for paying the blood money himself, then the reward for returning the fugitive slave is incumbent upon the master, because ultimately the slave's return benefits the master (the slave remains his property). Second, if the master instead surrenders the slave himself to the heirs of the slain as compensation (i.e., the slave becomes their property), then the reward for returning the slave falls upon those heirs, because they are the ones who benefit from the return. The ruling hinges on the principle that the party that reaps the benefit of the slave's return must bear the expense of the reward.

Key Terms
جعل (ju'l): The reward offered or paid for the return of a runaway slave.
مولی (mawla): The master or owner of the slave.
خطا (khata'): Mistake, unintentional act; here refers to accidental killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The heirs of the slain
B) The master
C) The retriever of the slave
D) No one

Key Takeaway
The obligation of ju'l follows the one who benefits from the slave's return.

Ju'l for a Gifted Runaway Slave
Ruling on ju'l for a gifted slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on ju'l for a gifted runaway slave and explain why the donee is liable.

Core Idea
The reward for returning a gifted slave is on the donee, not the donor, even if the gift is later revoked.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: a slave who has been gifted (hiba) runs away, and someone returns him for a reward (ju'l). Who owes the reward? The donor who gave the slave away, or the donee who received him? The Hanafi ruling clarifies that liability falls on the donee, because he is the one who benefited when the slave was returned to his possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The slave is a gift (mawhub). He runs away and is subsequently returned. A reward (ju'l) was promised for his return.
2
State the ruling
The reward is obligatory (wajib) upon the donee (mawhub lahu) – the person who received the slave as a gift.
Even if the donor later revokes the gift, the reward remains on the donee.
3
Understand the rationale
The benefit of the return accrued to the donee at the moment of return, because the slave was in his possession. The donor received no benefit from the return.
This is why subsequent revocation does not shift liability.
4
Consider the exception
If the donee had already relinquished control of the slave before the return (e.g., returned the slave to the donor), then the benefit might shift to the donor.
This is indicated by the phrase 'only when the donee terminates his control after the return'.
5
Apply to analogous situations
This principle applies to any gifted property that is later recovered: the donee at the time of recovery is liable for any reward promised, regardless of subsequent ownership changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابق موہوب ہے تو جعل موہولہ پر ہے
وَإِنْ كَانَ مَوْهُو بَا فَعَلَى الْمَوْهُوبِ لَهُ وَإِنْ رَجَعَ الْوَاهِبُ فِي هِبَتِهِ بَعْدَ الرَّدْ لِأَنَّ الْمُنفَعَةَ لِلْوَاهِبِ مَا حَصَلَتْ ردِبَل بِتَرْكِ المَوهُوبِ لَهُ التَّصَرُّفَ فِيهِ بَعْدَ الرَّد
ترجمہ اور اگر یہ غلام ہبہ کیا ہوا ہو تو اس کا جعل اسی پر لازم ہو گا جسے وہ غلام ہبہ کے طور پر دے دیا گیا ہو۔ اگر چہ واپسی کے بعد مبہ کرنے والا اپنا ہبہ واپس لے لے کیونکہ اس کی واپسی سے ہبہ کرنے والے کو کچھ بھی فائدہ نہیں ہوا ۔ بلکہ اسی وقت اسے فائدہ ہوگا جبکہ موہوب لہ نے یعنی جسے ہبہ کیا گیا تھا اپنا اختیار اس سے ختم کر دیا ہو۔
If the slave is gifted, then the reward is on the donee. And if the slave is gifted, then the reward is on the donee, even if the donor takes back his gift after the return because the benefit did not accrue to the donor, but only when the donee relinquishes control after the return. Commentary: And if this slave was given as a gift, then the reward is obligatory upon the one to whom the slave was given as a gift. Even if after the return the donor takes back his gift, because no benefit accrued to the donor from the return. Rather, benefit occurs only when the donee—i.e., the one who was given the gift—has terminated his control over it after the return.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a runaway slave who is gifted property (hiba). The Arabic matn (from al-Hidayah) states: If the slave was gifted (mawhub), then the reward (ju'l) is on the donee (al-mawhub lahu), even if the donor (al-wahib) revokes the gift after the return. The reason given is that the benefit of the return does not go to the donor; it goes to the donee at the time of return. The Urdu commentary clarifies: the reward is obligatory upon the donee. Even if the donor later takes the gift back, the reward is still on the donee because he was the one who benefited at the time of return (by having the slave in his possession). However, if the donee had already relinquished control (by returning the slave to the donor before the fugitive was brought back?), then the benefit might shift? The text says 'only when the donee terminates his control after the return', implying that if the donee had already surrendered the slave before retrieval, perhaps the donor benefits. But the primary ruling is clear: the ju'l is on the donee at the moment the slave is returned.

Key Terms
موہوب (mawhub): A slave who has been given as a gift (hiba).
موہوب لہ (mawhub lahu): The donee, the person to whom the slave was gifted.
واہب (wahib): The donor, the person who gave the gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A gifted runaway slave is returned. The donor later revokes the gift. Who is liable for the reward (ju'l)?
A) The donor, because he regains ownership
B) The donee, because benefit was at the time of return
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
In a ju'l contract for a gifted runaway slave, the reward is wajib on the donee, not the donor, because benefit is assessed at the time of return.
